fill-rule="evenodd"></path></svg></a></li><li class="css-60hakz"><a aria-label="Email" href="mailto:?subject=NYTimes.com%3A%20For%20Finland%E2%80%99s%20President%20and%20Other%20Guests%20of%20Trump%2C%20Stoicism%20Is%20Key&amp;body=From%20The%20New%20York%20Times%3A%0A%0AFor%20Finland%E2%80%99s%20President%20and%20Other%20Guests%20of%20Trump%2C%20Stoicism%20Is%20Key%0A%0AA%20placid%20face%20and%20a%20willingness%20to%20expect%20the%20unexpected%20has%20become%20the%20price%20of%20admission%20for%20any%20foreign%20ally%20who%20hopes%20for%20a%20productive%20audience%20with%20President%20Trump.%0A%0Ahttps%3A%2F%2Fwww.nytimes.com%2F2019%2F10%2F02%2Fus%2Fpolitics%2Ftrump-press-conferences.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><svg class="css-4brsb6" height="9" viewbox="0 0 15 9" width="15"><path clip-rule="evenodd" d="M.906 8.418V0L5.64 4.76.906 8.419zm13 0L9.174 4.761 13.906 0v8.418zM7.407 6.539l-1.13-1.137L.907 9h13l-5.37-3.598-1.13 1.137zM1.297 0h12.22l-6.11 5.095L1.297 0z" fill="#000" fill-rule="evenodd"></path></svg></a></li><li class="css-60hakz"><div class="css-6n7j50"><button aria-expanded="false" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="More sharing options" class="css-16ogagc" data-testid=""><svg class="css-uhuo44" height="13" viewbox="0 0 16 13" width="16"><path clip-rule="evenodd" d="M15.406 5.359L8.978 0v3.215C3.82 3.215.406 8.107.406 12.66 1.653 9.133 4.29 7.517 8.978 7.517v3.2l6.428-5.358z" fill="#000" fill-rule="evenodd"></path></svg></button></div></li><li class="css-60hakz"></li></ul></div></div></li></ul></div></header></div><section class="meteredContent css-1i2y565" itemprop="articleBody" name="articleBody"><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">WASHINGTON — An <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2017/07/14/us/politics/president-donald-trump-handshakes.html?module=inline" title="">awkward handshake</a> is really the least of their worries. </p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">As President Trump continues to rage against impeachment — and the Democrats and whistle-blower he holds responsible for bringing it about — visiting world leaders are encountering a different kind of diplomatic mission.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">It includes a welcome ceremony, a meeting with Mr. Trump and an invitation to sit stone-faced for an indeterminate amount of time on live television as the <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/10/01/us/politics/trump-treason-impeachment.html?module=inline" title="">president accuses people of treason</a>, lies and corruption. And sometimes the session is reprised a little later in a formal news conference.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">That was what happened on Wednesday when President Sauli Niinisto of Finland became the latest foreign leader to strike a straight-lipped contrast to Mr. Trump as Mr. Trump defended himself and attacked his adversaries. Not once but twice.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">As reporters crowded into the Oval Office, Mr. Trump sat beside his guest and accused Democratic lawmakers, including Representative Adam B. Schiff, the chairman of the House Intelligence Committee, of treason. Mr. Trump also suggested that the congressman was not fit to carry the secretary of state’s “‘blank’ strap,” as Mr. Niinisto looked on. </p></div><aside aria-hidden="false" aria-label="companion column" class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“He should resign from office in disgrace,” Mr. Trump said of Mr. Schiff, “and frankly they should look at him for treason.”</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Adding to the awkward scene, a Finnish reporter seemed to pick up on the president’s anger, and asked Mr. Trump what he could learn from Finland, which has been <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.cnn.com/travel/article/worlds-happiest-countries-united-nations-2019/index.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank" title="">rated the happiest country in the world</a>. </p></div><aside aria-hidden="false" aria-label="companion column" class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-cfo9c3"></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“Finland is a happy country,” Mr. Trump said in response as he slapped Mr. Niinisto’s knee. “Finland is a happy country. He’s a happy leader, too.”</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Mr. Niinisto nodded and seemingly moved to swat Mr. Trump’s hand away. </p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">But the American president wasn’t done. And at a news conference later Wednesday, Mr. Niinisto was all but forced to again express some stolid Nordic enthusiasm. </p></div><aside aria-hidden="false" aria-label="companion column" class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“Mr. President, you have here a great democracy,” Mr. Niinisto told Mr. Trump in the East Room. “Keep it going on.”</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Skipping the usual protocol with a visiting foreign leader is nothing new for Mr. Trump. </p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">He has launched into meandering asides, including <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://twitter.com/tommyxtopher/status/1113151453554769920?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw%7Ctwcamp%5Etweetembed%7Ctwterm%5E1113151453554769920&amp;ref_url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.vox.com%2F2019%2F4%2F2%2F18292571%2Ftrump-nato-secretary-white-house-oranges" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank" title="">falsely claiming his father was born in Germany</a> as Jens Stoltenberg, the NATO secretary general, looked on in April. In 2017, he seemed to forget <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.cnn.com/2017/03/17/politics/donald-trump-angela-merkel-handshake/index.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank" title="">to shake hands</a> with Angela Merkel, the German chancellor.</p></div><aside aria-hidden="false" aria-label="companion column" class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-79elbk" data-testid="photoviewer-wrapper"><div class="css-z3e15g" data-testid="photoviewer-wrapper-hidden"></div><div class="css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15" data-testid="photoviewer-children"><figure aria-label="media" class="css-1ef8w8q e1g7ppur0" itemid="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/10/02/us/politics/02dc-memo-02/02dc-memo-02-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp" itemprop="associatedMedia" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" role="group"><div class="css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0"><span class="css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0">Image</span><img alt="President Trump last year with President Muhammadu Buhari of Nigeria." class="css-1m50asq" itemid="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/10/02/us/politics/02dc-memo-02/02dc-memo-02-articleLarge.jpg?quality=75&amp;auto=webp&amp;disable=upscale" itemprop="url" sizes="((min-width: 600px) and (max-width: 1004px)) 84vw, (min-width: 1005px) 80vw, 100vw" src="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/10/02/us/politics/02dc-memo-02/02dc-memo-02-articleLarge.jpg?quality=75&amp;auto=webp&amp;disable=upscale" srcset="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/10/02/us/politics/02dc-memo-02/02dc-memo-02-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 600w,https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/10/02/us/politics/02dc-memo-02/02dc-memo-02-jumbo.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 1024w,https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/10/02/us/politics/02dc-memo-02/02dc-memo-02-superJumbo.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 2048w"/></div><figcaption class="css-18crmh6 e1xdpqjp0" itemprop="caption description"><span aria-hidden="true" class="css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0">President Trump last year with President Muhammadu Buhari of Nigeria.</span><span class="css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90" itemprop="copyrightHolder"><span class="css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0">Credit</span><span>Tom Brenner/The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">And, in front of Muhammadu Buhari, the president of Nigeria, Mr. Trump <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2018/01/11/us/politics/trump-shithole-countries.html?module=inline" title="">took questions concerning reports</a> that he had called several African nations “shithole countries.” </p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“We didn’t discuss it because the president knows me,” Mr. Trump told reporters during his news conference with Mr. Buhari in April 2018, “and he knows where I’m coming from, and I appreciate that.”</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Faced with the same question, the Nigerian president demurred, saying “the best thing for me is to keep quiet.”</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Since the beginning of Mr. Trump’s presidency, at least some world leaders and their aides have made it a point to anticipate unexpected moments like these and plan ahead, according to a former official in the Washington diplomatic community who spoke on the condition of anonymity to not describe private planning. </p></div><aside aria-hidden="false" aria-label="companion column" class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">The president’s approach has bent the norms of a protocol system put in place by Mr. Trump’s modern predecessors, according to Peter Selfridge, who served as the United States chief of protocol during the Obama administration. </p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“Obviously,” Mr. Selfridge said, “this president uses the press conference a little differently.”</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">President Barack Obama would regularly give his diplomatic guests warnings that a press availability might contain off-topic questions, according to a former Obama administration official who spoke on the condition of anonymity. But Mr. Obama would also appear visibly annoyed when asked questions not related to the purpose of the visit, especially if he was abroad. </p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">When asked if Mr. Trump gave his visitors a similar heads-up, Stephanie Grisham, the White House press secretary, indicated that there was no need. </p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“I think foreign leaders are well aware that the U.S. press corps often has no desire to cover the foreign diplomacy taking place during these visits,” Ms. Grisham wrote in an email. </p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Indeed, Mr. Trump’s behavior often overshadows whatever diplomacy is taking place. White House officials told journalists before Mr. Niinisto’s visit that it would focus on economic cooperation and mutual security concerns between the two countries, which is a familiar refrain before any such visit. </p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">But in the past two weeks, impeachment and the allegations against Mr. Trump and his relations with Ukraine have overshadowed diplomatic concerns.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">That was more than just subtext to Mr. Trump’s meeting last week in New York with Volodymyr Zelensky, the Ukrainian president. Mr. Zelensky, who in a transcript of his phone call with Mr. Trump in July adeptly flattered the president, could barely mask his discomfort when the two met with reporters afterward.</p></div><aside aria-hidden="false" aria-label="companion column" class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“It’s a great pleasure to me to be here,” Mr. Zelensky said, “and it’s better to be on TV than by phone, I think.” </p></div><aside aria-hidden="false" aria-label="companion column" class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">And two weeks ago, <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/20/us/politics/scott-morrison-trump-administration-hosts-second-state-dinner.html?module=inline" title="">Scott Morrison, the prime minister of Australia</a>, had little time to prepare when his state visit came just as the furor over the president and Ukraine began to unfold. </p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">After Mr. Morrison’s welcome ceremony, Mr. Trump pulled him into the Oval Office and began deriding the <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/20/us/politics/trump-whistle-blower-ukraine.html?module=inline" title="">whistle-blower’s complaint that details</a> him repeatedly pressing the Ukrainian president to talk with aides interested in an investigation of former Vice President Joseph R. Biden Jr. </p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Defending his behavior on the call, he turned to Mr. Morrison for support.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“I’ve had conversations with many leaders,” Mr. Trump said. “They’re always appropriate. I think Scott can tell you that.”</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0"> </p></div><aside aria-hidden="false" aria-label="companion column" class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div></section><div covering the cultural impact of the Trump administration on the nation's capital and beyond. <span class="css-4w91ra"> <a class="css-1rj8to8" href="https://twitter.com/katierogers" rel="noopener 1-.9c.6.5 1.1.9 2.5 1v8.3L44 3.2c-.5-.8-1.2-1.9-2.6-1.9-1.6 0-3 1.4-2.8 3.6h.3c.1-.6.4-1.3 1.1-1.3.5 0 1 .5 1.3 1v3.3c-1.8 0-3 .8-3 2.3 0 .8.4 2 1.6 2.3v-.2c-.2-.2-.3-.4-.3-.7 0-.5.4-.9 <div id="RavenInstaller">
<script>
if (window.INSTALL_RAVEN) {
  window.addEventListener('load', function(event) {
    var includeRaven = document.getElementById("RavenInstaller");
    var script = document.createElement("script");
    script.src = "/vi-assets/static-assets/raven.min-830a6d04a55c283934dd1893d6ddc66d.js";
    script.onload = function() {
      /* eslint-disable */
// Install Raven
window.Raven.config('https://7bc8bccf5c254286a99b11c68f6bf4ce@sentry.io/178860', {
  release: vi.env.RELEASE,
  environment: vi.env.ENVIRONMENT,
  ignoreErrors: [/SecurityError: Blocked a frame with origin.*/]
}).install(); // Stop using our error handler

window.nyt_errors.ravenInstalled = true;
var regex = /nyt-a=(.*?)(;|$)/;
var id = regex.exec(document.cookie);

if (id !== null) {
  id = id[1];
} else {
  id = '';
} // Setting nyt-a as user context


window.Raven.setUserContext({
  id: id
}); // Pass collected errors to Raven

window.nyt_errors.list.forEach(function (err) {
  // weird?
  if (!err) {
    return;
  } // also weird ... ?


  if (!err.err) {
    // maybe err itself is an Error?
    if (err instanceof Error) {
      window.Raven.captureException(err, err.data || {});
    } // else { silently ignore? }

  } // just making sure ...


  if (err.err instanceof Error) {
    window.Raven.captureException(err.err, err.data || {});
  } // else { silently ignore? }

}); // Pass collected Tags to Raven

window.nyt_errors.tags.forEach(function (tag) {
  window.Raven.setTagsContext(tag);
});
    };
    includeRaven.appendChild(script);
  });
}
</script>
